After the Water Price of Tap Water is Reduced by 20% 131

It is Said that the People's Price

Is Still Below the Production Cost

The Public Relations Office of the Public Concession Board of Directors released a statement saying that a news item about the tap water price published in various newspapers in the city on the 28th of last month was not in line with the facts. The relevant parties issued the following statement yesterday:

Since April of last year, the public concession's tap water has implemented a scientific water rate calculated by water meters, with the intention of providing relief to poor users. However, last year, some alleyway houses consumed a large amount of water, and the fees were paid by the landlords, who were temporarily given a discount. At the end of the year, a survey found that more than half of these alleyway houses had landlords whose water fees were within 7.5% of the rental value. The current water price has no other discount except for the recently announced 20% discount to be implemented from April 1 of this year. The 20% discount is a uniform reduction of 20% on the bill. If the consumption of various alleyway houses is the same as last year, then after the 20% discount is implemented, it is estimated that about 65 out of every 100 alleyway houses will have water fees that are below 7.5% of the rental value. The production cost of the tap water company, including capital interest and operating expenses, is 3.1 cents per thousand gallons. After the 20% discount, for those with a rent of 25 yuan or less, the water price paid per thousand gallons is still less than 3.1 cents. This type of tenant accounts for about 400,000 people, which shows that a large portion of the citizens are paying a price for water that is still below the production cost.

Li Pingheng and Cheng Haifeng Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday 132

Discussing the Implementation Steps of Factory Inspection

After the Central Factory Inspection Office decided on the implementation procedures for factory inspection and promoted it in five stages, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau was ordered to comply. Li Pingheng, Director of the Labor Department of the Ministry of Industry, and Cheng Haifeng, Section Chief of the Inspection Office, arrived in Shanghai yesterday. The details are as follows:

The City Complies

After the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau received the Municipal Government's order to forward the implementation procedures for factory inspection, it immediately handed it over to the Factory Inspection Section for compliance. A reporter from the New Voice Society met with Tian Heqing, Director of the Factory Inspection Section of the Social Affairs Bureau, yesterday. According to him, the factory inspection will be carried out in stages in accordance with the procedures prescribed by the Central Factory Inspection Office. As for the various tasks specified in the first stage, some have already been implemented within the urban area, and it has now been decided to handle them separately in accordance with the various items specified in the first stage.

Arrived in Shanghai for Negotiations

Li Pingheng, Director of the Labor Department of the Ministry of Industry, and Cheng Haifeng, Section Chief of the Central Factory Inspection Office, arrived in Shanghai together from Beijing yesterday morning. At 3:00 p.m. yesterday, Cheng Haifeng went to the city center to discuss Shanghai factory inspection matters with Tian Heqing, Director of the Factory Inspection Section of the Social Affairs Bureau, and others. The meeting ended at 5:00 p.m. It is reported that at the upcoming International Labor Conference, Li Pingheng will represent the government, and Cheng Haifeng will be the advisor to labor representative An Futing. They will also sail from Shanghai on the Italian ship Conte Rosso on the 10th of this month.

Implementation Steps

A reporter from the New Voice Society met with Cheng Haifeng at the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday. According to him, the Central Factory Inspection Office, in view of the fact that China's factory production is not only backward but also declining, has specially formulated the implementation procedures for factory inspection and is promoting it in stages. However, the necessary steps for implementing factory inspection are: (1) Explanation: Explain the Factory Law to both labor and management in each factory so that they obey and comply with it. (2) Persuasion: If the factories do not make corrections after the explanation, they will be persuaded to make corrections. (3) Warning: If the factories still do not make corrections after being persuaded, they will be warned. (4) Punishment: If the factories do not listen to the warning, they will be punished according to the law. The above items are all educational work to make the factories understand, so that the implementation of factory inspection is easier, and so on.

Qian Chengxu Discusses Trademark Opinions 133

According to the Central News Agency, after several days of exchanging opinions between the industrial and commercial circles on the issue of trademark recognition of font and non-recognition of pronunciation, it is believed that for domestic goods factories whose trademarks have already gained a considerable position in the market, most advocate that in addition to the font, there must be appropriate remedies for the pronunciation. If this proposition is to be thoroughly implemented, the trademark law must be fundamentally revised. Yesterday, the reporter interviewed Qian Chengxu of the China General Chamber of Industry, asking for his opinion on this legal amendment and how it can be remedied. Today, the Ministry of Justice has established a statutory interpretation. According to Qian, "I went to Beijing the day before yesterday and discussed this matter several times with the government, but the opinions were not consistent. Therefore, the Ministry of Industry will send Director Liang Shangdong to Shanghai in the coming days to discuss it with the industrial and commercial circles. In my personal opinion, although Western trademark laws all recognize the font but not the pronunciation, Western alphabets have a fixed pronunciation. Besides this one sound, it is difficult to find a second sound. Therefore, in fact, it emphasizes the form, but the pronunciation does not change, which means that it recognizes the form and the pronunciation, emphasizing both directly and indirectly. The law does not need to add any regulations on the point of recognizing the pronunciation. However, in the Chinese language, one sound can find many characters with the same meaning. At this time when domestic goods are not yet developed, advocating equal emphasis on sound and form does not seem to be without a reasonable reason. In short, in all circumstances, the representative of the Ministry of Industry will come to Shanghai in the coming days, and everyone can discuss it in detail. During this period, the China General Chamber of Industry has sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and various trade associations and companies, asking them to sign their opinions. Once all the opinions are collected, a meeting will be held to jointly study the matter with the representative of the Ministry of Industry."

The Number of Vendors at the Jing'an Temple Fair This Year Will Be Restricted 135

The Jing'an Temple Bathing Buddha Festival Fair was recently discussed by the Concession Bureau's Security Committee. According to the police department's report, the location of the stalls this year will be designated by the Works Department, and more police officers will be dispatched to patrol in order to prevent encroachment. If the Concession Bureau issues a public announcement, the abbot is willing to issue licenses to the vendors in order to facilitate the crackdown. The number of stalls at the fair was 3,000 in 1932 and increased to 4,700 last year. The original intention of the fair was for villagers to sell their products, but in recent years, the vendors have often been residents of the concession or Nanshi in the city, which is contrary to the original intention. The Concession Bureau has been paying attention to the restriction of stalls for many years, so the committee, after deliberation, agreed that the fair should be limited to genuine villagers selling their handmade goods and, in view of the needs of public health and traffic convenience, it is proposed to follow the police department's proposal: (1) Limit the number of stalls to 1,500 and only allow the sale of handmade goods. (2) Announce this decision as soon as possible and order the police department and the abbot of the temple to agree on a detailed plan. This case was submitted to the Board of Directors of the Concession Bureau on April 4 and was approved.

Two Mounds Leveled, Remains' Whereabouts Unknown

Spring Outing Car Accident on the Shanghai-Hangzhou Highway 137

Seven Chinese Passengers Plunge into a Small River

Westerners Rescue with a Small Boat

The *North China Daily News* reports that during the Easter holidays, Westerners from this port flocked to Hangzhou for sightseeing. Mr. and Mrs. Barraclough were among them. After their trip, the Barracloughs were returning to Shanghai by car on Sunday when a large car carrying seven Chinese passengers sped past them. After passing Minhang by about three miles, the car, for some unknown reason, suddenly veered off the road, crossed a steep embankment, and plunged into a small river beside the road. Shortly after, the Barracloughs' car arrived and saw five Chinese standing on the side of the car in the river. Two others, unable to climb out, were sitting on the car cushions with only their heads above the water. Several farmers stood on the embankment, watching from a distance. The Barracloughs, after arriving at the scene, were soon joined by several other foreigners. They worked together to carry out the rescue, finding a small boat to bring everyone ashore. When asked about the incident last night, Mr. Barraclough replied that he could not find anyone who witnessed the accident, so he did not know the details. The people who fell into the river were too shocked to recount what happened. It seems that the windows of the car were closed, allowing the people inside to open the doors and climb out before the car filled with water. Everyone suffered minor injuries and was sent to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment. According to the hospital, most of the injuries were scrapes and cuts. However, one woman had three teeth knocked out, and one man suffered severe eye injuries that may lead to blindness.

Shanghai-Nanjing-Suzhou Tobacco and Alcohol Joint Association Sends Letters Urging Member Groups to Pay Fees 142

Otherwise, the Association's Finances Will Be Unsustainable, Leading to Dissolution

The Fiscal Year Is Approaching, Tax Regulations May Be Changed, Responsibilities Are Heavy

The Shanghai-Nanjing-Suzhou Tobacco and Alcohol Industry Association was established last year during the tax bureau's reform of new regulations. At that time, the tobacco and alcohol industry associations in various cities and counties believed that the new regulations were harmful and disruptive to businesses, and they strongly advocated for reform. However, due to legal restrictions, their efforts were unsuccessful. Recently, member groups have been even more in arrears with their membership fees, resulting in financial difficulties for the association and making it unsustainable. It was decided to appoint economic committee members in different districts to be responsible for collecting fees. Yesterday, Dai Zhuo'an, standing committee member and economic committee member for the eighth district, sent a letter to the economic committee members of each district, explaining that in the coming year, tax authorities, due to unsatisfactory tax revenue reforms, will once again change the plan. The work of the joint association remains very important. He hoped to explain the advantages and disadvantages to each member group, and jointly maintain the overall situation. The original letter said: "Dear Sirs, it has been nine months since the establishment of our association. Economic expenditures have been increasingly difficult, resulting in a deficit of over 2,600 yuan. If we count on collecting over 2,000 yuan in membership fees by the spring to offset the deficit, the actual loss is no more than 600 yuan. The collection of membership fees has been difficult, with many owing for the autumn and winter seasons. Without funds, how can the association survive? The temporary general meeting of members decided to organize an economic committee, dividing it into eight districts, to be responsible for urging payment. Committee members for each district were appointed by the members of each district present, and recorded. Furthermore, the economic committee decided that the association will print and distribute the pledge forms, along with the list of member representatives of the tobacco and alcohol associations in each district, the original amount of membership fees, and the overdue fee slips, separately. All are to be returned to the association within 20 days, so as to have a comprehensive plan. If there is still no solution by the deadline, the joint association will be dissolved. It is noted that the tobacco and alcohol industries exist everywhere. If they are like a plate of loose sand, since the founding of the Republic, donations and taxes have been repeatedly increased, with no end in sight. Being taken from and demanded from, being at the mercy of others, is all due to the lack of a united resistance. Last year, the associations of Shanghai City worked hard to rise up, loudly calling for action, which led to the organization of the Shanghai-Nanjing-Suzhou Tobacco and Alcohol Joint Association. At the inaugural meeting, more than a hundred associations participated, a passionate display that greatly enhanced the reputation of tobacco and alcohol merchants. How long ago was it that it has now fallen into a difficult state due to financial problems? Those who do not know the details will certainly say it is a 'five-minute fever'. In fact, it is not entirely so. In my opinion, there are other reasons. At the beginning of the association's establishment, the members had greater hopes. At that time, the tax regulations were being changed. The association worked for several months, but the goal was not achieved, which must have dissatisfied the majority of members. In fact, the change of regulations at that time was due to the arbitrary and self-willed actions of the former tax commissioner, Xie Qi, who announced and implemented the regulations with lightning speed during the annual handover, making it fundamentally difficult to overturn. However, the association repeatedly sent representatives to various places to petition, running around and appealing, and ultimately managed to force changes in the harsh regulations. The work was not without effort. If there had been no joint association to take the lead, the suffering of tobacco and alcohol merchants everywhere from the harsh treatment of tax collectors would have been unimaginable. In human affairs, there are tangible benefits and intangible benefits. Since its establishment, the association, even if it has achieved little, can be considered blameless. We agreed in the beginning and should be determined. We must not sit back and watch it dissolve because its effects are not significant. Think about it, if the joint association were to disappear, outsiders would laugh at our inability to unite, and we would be at the mercy of others, which is to be expected. Moreover, there are only three months left until the end of the year. Due to the changes in the regulations this year, merchants have suffered greatly, and tax revenues have actually fallen short. The competent authorities should also be aware that reform is not a good plan. Knowledgeable people expect that the policy will still be changed next year. Therefore, requesting improvements to the tax regulations and seeking various benefits for the industry is of great importance to the association. Nothing can be done without money. If the association's finances are unsustainable, how can it be supported? The decision to print and distribute pledge forms, asking each association to fill them out, is a kind of test to see whether each member has the sincerity to support the joint association. In other words, if they all give up, the joint association will also disappear and will no longer be maintained. The matter concerns the interests of the industry in the three provinces and cities of Shanghai, Nanjing, and Suzhou. I dare not remain silent. I sincerely state this directly, and I am confident that you will agree in the beginning and will certainly maintain it in the end. I hope that you will communicate my humble opinion to each member of your district, and promptly fill out the pledge forms and send them to the association. The amount owed for the autumn and winter seasons, along with the spring and summer membership fees that should be paid, is not much, and I believe it will not be difficult to arrange. I urge you to supervise and send them to the association by the deadline to provide assistance. The matter concerns public welfare, so please do not disregard or put it aside. This is my earnest prayer."

The Over-Year-Long "Butterfly" Trademark Case Concludes 143

Ms. Hu Die's Portrait Trademark Approved for Registration

The case between the Huanan Chemical Industry Company and the Family Industry Company over the "Butterfly" trademark dispute has been ongoing for over a year, with both parties repeatedly litigating. Previously, the Huanan Chemical Industry Company specially hired lawyer Zhang Shizhao to file an administrative appeal with the Executive Yuan according to law. The Executive Yuan has now decided that Ms. Hu Die's portrait trademark should be approved for registration according to law. The full text of the original decision is transcribed as follows: Executive Yuan Decision Document, Su Zi No. 8, [Main Text] The original disposition and the original decision are both revoked. The re-appellant's ["Ms. Hu Die Portrait"] trademark is approved for registration according to law. [Facts] The re-appellant previously applied for registration of four ["Ms. Hu Die Portrait"] trademarks, respectively used for tooth powder and toothpaste, which were approved and listed under numbers 12924, 12925, 12926, and 12927. Subsequently, the Family Industry Company claimed that the four trademarks imitated its registered numbers 210 ["Meili"], 3586 ["Circular Half-Body Woman"], 10717 ["Invincible Brand Chinese and Western"], and four applications for registration of ["Butterfly Chinese and Western"], 209 ["Invincible Brand"], and approved number 13173 ["Butterfly Chinese and Western"] trademarks for similar products, and filed an objection with the Trademark Bureau. The bureau, believing that the characters ["Hu Die"] in the re-appellant's trademark were likely to be confused in pronunciation with the characters ["Invincible"] of the Family Industry Company's Invincible Brand, revoked the registration of the re-appellant's trademark. The re-appellant requested a review of the objection, but it was rejected. Dissatisfied with this disposition, they appealed to the Ministry of Industry. The ministry, referring to various relevant documents from the former Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce and the former Trademark Bureau, which stated that ["Invincible Brand is Butterfly Brand"] and ["Invincible Brand is commonly known as Butterfly Brand"], held that the two characters ["Hu Die"] and ["Butterfly"] were completely indistinguishable, and confusion was unavoidable in transactions, so the appeal was rejected. The re-appellant was still not satisfied and filed a further appeal with the Executive Yuan. [Reasoning] In this case, the characters, graphics, symbols, and colors used in the ["Ms. Hu Die Portrait"] trademark in dispute by the re-appellant are not identical to the various trademarks of the Family Industry Company's Invincible Brand. What should be examined is whether the homophony between ["Hu Die Brand"] and ["Invincible Brand"] can be a reason for not allowing registration, and whether ["Invincible Brand is Butterfly Brand"] can exclude the registration of the ["Ms. Hu Die Portrait"] trademark. The pronunciation of the two characters ["Invincible"] and ["Hu Die"] is not without similarity, but the characters in trademark law only refer to the form they represent, and do not include the pronunciation, as explained in interpretations 1003 and 1044 of the Judicial Yuan. If the re-appellant's trademark in dispute is not allowed to be registered because the two characters ["Hu Die"] and ["Invincible"] are homophones, it would be inconsistent with the interpretations of the Judicial Yuan. Furthermore, the re-appellant previously applied for registration using the two characters ["Hu Die"], which was revoked by the Trademark Bureau. They then modified the two characters ["Hu Die"] to the six characters ["Ms. Hu Die Portrait"] to apply for registration as the trademark name. Thus, ["Ms. Hu Die Portrait"] has become a complete trademark name, which can be distinguished from the Family Industry Company's ["Invincible Brand, commonly known as Butterfly Brand"] in writing, and it is naturally difficult to not allow its registration according to law. The Trademark Bureau's rejection of the re-appellant's trademark registration, and the Ministry of Industry's rejection of its appeal, are improper. However, when the re-appellant actually uses the trademark, only the two characters ["Hu Die"] are written, which should be corrected. Subsequently, the re-appellant should indicate the six characters ["Ms. Hu Die Portrait"] on the trademark to comply with the original case. Based on the above conclusions, the appeal is justified, and the decision is made in accordance with the first paragraph of Article 9 of the Appeal Law as stated in the main text.

Cracking Down on Extra Demands by Porters on Both Railways 145

A Flat Rate of Twelve Copper Coins Per Piece

The Two Railways Transportation Department, noting that porters at various stations, despite repeated strict prohibitions against extra demands, continue to engage in such behavior, which harms the railway's reputation, has organized a committee to crack down on extra demands by porters, and has studied effective methods of crackdown, resulting in the following three resolutions: (1) Regarding the re-determination of porterage fees, it was resolved: (a) The porterage fee for luggage, regardless of distance or weight, shall be a flat rate of twelve copper coins per piece. (b) This porterage fee refers to the service of carrying luggage from outside the station gate to the baggage room, and then from the baggage room to the train, or from the train to the baggage room, and then from the baggage room to outside the station gate. (c) The porterage fee for packages shall be eight copper coins per piece for packages weighing 60 kilograms or less, and twelve copper coins per piece for packages weighing more than 60 kilograms up to 120 kilograms. (2) Regarding how to crack down on porters rushing onto trains or competing to carry luggage, it was resolved that the personnel in charge at each station must evenly distribute the daily porterage fees collected, so that porters have equal treatment. (3) Regarding cracking down on porters extorting passengers, it was resolved: (a) Prepare a price list for baggage delivery, clearly stating "Baggage delivery: twelve copper coins per piece," and "If there are extra demands, please bring this card to the stationmaster." The card should also indicate the porter's number, and be issued to each porter for use. When carrying luggage, whether entering or leaving the station, the porter must hand the card to the passenger, who will pay the porter according to the price list after all procedures are completed, and return the card to the porter. If there are extra demands, the passenger can bring the card to the stationmaster. If a porter fails to hand the card to the passenger when carrying luggage, they should be severely punished immediately. (b) Advertise as much as possible to the public, so that passengers know to ask the porter for the card when hiring a porter to carry luggage. (c) If a porter extorts a passenger, they should be immediately dismissed, and a photo taken and posted at major stations, never to be employed again. (d) The porter's uniform should state "Baggage delivery: twelve copper coins per piece." (e) The stationmaster's office should have a photo of each porter, with their name and number noted. Every morning and afternoon, the person in charge should report the number and number of porters on duty to the stationmaster. If it is found that the number does not match, they should be dismissed immediately.

The Xu Case Committee Members Accused of Insulting the Court's Judgment 146

Ye Jiaxing Absent, Rescheduled for Further Questioning

Wang Honghui and Others Fined 200 Yuan Each

The five committee members of the Xu Case Support Association who were accused were tried yesterday afternoon in the eighth courtroom of the First Special District Local Court by Judge Zhan Liangce. Beforehand, to maintain order and prevent irrelevant people from entering the courtroom, the court authorities specially dispatched several Chinese and Western detectives from the Municipal Council Police to assist. The visitor seats were unusually empty, so the courtroom was extremely quiet. First, Judge Zhan asked the four defendants their names, ages, residences, and occupations. This time, he received a telegram from the division headquarters and immediately went to Beijing, and submitted the commission to the court. Judge Zhan, since Ye had not surrendered, immediately began questioning the other four defendants. First, Wang Honghui was brought to the stand. He was informed that the prosecutor had charged him with publicly insulting a public office in accordance with Article 146, Section 2 of the Criminal Code, and that he should have received the indictment. He was asked if he had any defense to offer today. Wang Honghui replied that the Xu Case Committee members were nominated by others, not something he wanted to do. On January 16, after the rent reduction meeting ended, he left the meeting. He was not present at the subsequent Xu Case meeting. He claimed not to know about anything. The court then asked when the Xu Case Committee was established, who the committee members were, what work they did, and who drafted the declaration for the first executive committee meeting on January 20, which nominated him as secretary. Wang generally replied that he did not know or did not pay attention. Next, Huang Hanliang was called, and he was also informed of the legal articles he was accused of violating. Huang Hanliang then argued that he was originally a member of the presidium at the January 16 rent reduction meeting. By the time the discussion was over, he was already mentally exhausted, so he left the meeting. He did not participate in the subsequent expulsion meeting. Although the *Min Bao* newspaper reported that he was nominated as a committee member, he did not read the *Min Bao* and did not know about it at the time. Only after being summoned for investigation did he find out. He had already published a statement in the newspaper on March 19 after the investigation. What he wants to say is all in the newspaper. Then, he presented a newspaper. The court subsequently asked about the petition to the Ministry of Justice in Beijing, but he flatly denied it, claiming that he went to Beijing by night train on February 20, falsely claiming it was a rent reduction issue. Then, Xue Guangqian was called for questioning. Xue stated that he had two points to defend regarding the accusation: (1) Regarding the Xu Case Committee part, he left the rent reduction meeting that day. He was arrested as a Xu Case Committee member, which he was informed of the next day by a friend named Zhang. However, he had already sent a letter of resignation on the 18th and had never participated. (2) Regarding the petition to Beijing part, he stated that on the date he was accused of going to Beijing, he was actually working at the Social Affairs Bureau. In addition to the Social Affairs Bureau providing proof for him, he had submitted to the Ministry of Justice his identification and attached his photo requesting recognition of his appearance. It was possible that someone was using his name. Finally, Li Ruzhang was questioned. Li confessed that although he was nominated as a committee member, he did not take office and could not be held responsible. He also claimed that he was sick at home on February 21 and never went to Beijing. After Judge Zhan finished questioning, believing that the case was clear, he ordered the debate to begin. Prosecutor Zhong then stood up to argue, stating that Ye Jiaxing's part would be handled after he arrives. The remaining four defendants, based on the results of the investigation, were clearly important members of the Xu Case Committee and should be responsible for the declaration. He requested that they be punished according to law. The lawyers of each defendant also debated in turn. The court then announced the verdict: except for Ye Jiaxing, whose questioning was rescheduled, the remaining four defendants were jointly found guilty of publicly insulting a public office and were each fined 200 yuan. If they chose to convert the fine into imprisonment, each three yuan would offset one day of imprisonment.

Lixin Accounting Firm Seeks Opinions on Accounting Terminology 149

And Presents a Newly Published Translation of Accounting Terms

The staff of the Lixin Accounting Firm in Shanghai are dedicated to the study of accounting theory. They believe that the current state of accounting terms in China is confusing and complex, and has not yet been standardized, causing inconvenience in both academic and business circles. Therefore, the firm's accountants, editorial staff, and school staff jointly formed an accounting terminology discussion group to research accounting terms. After a year of work, they compiled a "Translation of Accounting Terms," which contains over 2,200 English accounting terms and their research findings. The book lists all existing accounting terms from various published Chinese accounting books, as well as terms created and proposed by the firm itself, for comparison. The book has now been published, and the firm is distributing it to public and private institutions or individuals interested in studying accounting. At the same time, it is soliciting opinions from the national accounting academic and business communities on these translations. The announcement by Pan Xulun, the head accountant of the firm, is transcribed below.

We believe that accounting theory in China is still in its infancy, and accounting terms have not yet been standardized. When reading existing accounting books, the terminology used is often inconsistent, causing inconvenience not only for accounting professionals in practice, but also making it difficult for accounting scholars to choose appropriate terms in their writing. This is a matter that urgently needs improvement in China's accounting field.

Our firm's staff have been serving in the accounting profession for ten years and have always been dedicated to promoting accounting theory and improving accounting practice in China. Currently, while compiling the "Lixin Accounting Series" and the "Lixin Accounting Quarterly," we deeply feel the need to standardize accounting terms. Therefore, we have collected various translations from existing Chinese accounting books, and added to and compiled them, which was then reviewed and studied by the Lixin Accounting Terminology Discussion Group organized by our firm's staff, resulting in the "Translation of Accounting Terms" in two volumes. The book contains approximately 2,200 terms. In addition to listing the existing translations from various sources in China for comparison, the terms selected, proposed, or tentatively proposed by our firm's staff are also included.

However, we are aware that our staff's knowledge is limited and our understanding is incomplete. Furthermore, this work is of great importance to accounting theory and business in China, and it would be difficult to achieve perfection without soliciting broad opinions and gradually making corrections. Therefore, we are soliciting opinions from accounting experts across the country on these accounting terms, and we sincerely hope for your guidance.

On the one hand, our firm has printed an additional 1,000 copies of this book and will distribute them to all sectors for initial consideration. If any individuals or groups in China who are interested in studying accounting terms wish to request the book from our firm, please provide your name, address, and occupation, and we will send you two copies. One copy should be kept for your records, and we hope that you will mark the other copy with your suggestions for correction and return it to us as soon as possible, so that we can gather opinions, revise the original proposed translations, and publish them again, so that the confusing and complex accounting term translations in China can be gradually standardized. This is not only what our firm's staff hope for, but also what the entire accounting community in China would be fortunate to have. This is an announcement.

Banks and National Goods Companies

Organize One Hundred Sales Teams

Recently, due to the increasingly bleak world economic situation, the number of unemployed people has been increasing. Its nature is entirely to help unemployed small businessmen. The Ningbo Industrial Bank provides funds and lends money to small businessmen using economic credit methods, while the Shanghai National Goods Company is responsible for importing goods from various national goods manufacturers at cost and selling them to the sales teams, who then take them to the countryside to sell. The first step is to investigate the demand for domestic goods in the villages near Shanghai. The Shanghai National Goods Company will then purchase the goods on their behalf. The sales teams can profit, and the goods can penetrate the people. This is a business that is beneficial without harm, achieving multiple goals in one fell swoop.

Two More Cleaning Workers Arrested in West Shanghai Yesterday 155

Dagongshe reports that 19 cleaning workers in the Caojiadu area of West Shanghai were arrested and sent to the bureau for questioning the day before yesterday. Yesterday morning, at around 6 a.m., two more night soil collectors, Wang Aisheng and Little Monk, were pushing a night soil cart when they were spotted by a patrol officer on Jessfield Road in West Shanghai. The officer suspected that the workers were also involved in the disturbance, so he arrested them and sent them to the Sixth District Public Security Bureau for interrogation, after which they were returned to custody. Upon hearing the news, all the workers, because the Public Security Bureau had repeatedly arrested people, making it difficult to work with peace of mind, unanimously suspended work and requested assistance from Party and government agencies. The West Shanghai Cleaning Department, because the original night soil carters stopped working, which was a matter of public health, dismissed all the original workers and recruited new workers to replace them. The workers felt that the Cleaning Department disregarded their suffering and was illegally oppressing them, so they immediately convened a meeting and decided to: (1) petition the Party headquarters; (2) demand the restoration of their original jobs; (3) quickly release the arrested workers; (4) guarantee that the same incidents will not occur in the future; (5) if necessary, go to the Municipal Government to petition.

Children's Day Celebrated Throughout the Country 168

Qingdao (Qingdao, 4th) Today is Children's Day. Twenty schools participated, with over 4,000 students from the third grade and above. At 8:00 AM, they gathered at Shandong University for a costumed parade, followed by a commemorative ceremony in front of the City Hall, presided over by Director Lei, who reported on the significance of the day. Secretary Hu gave a speech on behalf of Shen Honglie. After the ceremony, they returned to Shandong University for a luncheon. The weather was clear and mild, and the participants sang songs along the way, creating a grand scene. Observers lined the streets.

Anqing (Anqing, 4th) The Department of Education summoned all primary schools in the city to hold a Children's Day celebration at the public sports field at 4:00 PM on the 4th. After that, the kindergarten games began and were interrupted by rain.

Taiyuan (Taiyuan, 4th) The Children's Day commemorative meeting in Taiyuan was held in Zhongshan Park on the morning of the 4th, with over 5,000 children and over 10,000 people attending, making it an unprecedented event. After the meeting, they marched and visited the two offices of Sui Province. Yan Xishan gave each child a can of food and a congratulatory message, and Xu Yongchang gave each child a pencil and a congratulatory message.

Hangzhou (Hangzhou) The Children's Day, jointly prepared by the Hangzhou Municipal Party and government agencies, was held at the Xinshichang Grand Theater on the morning of the 4th. More than 2,000 children and women participated. Chen Wen, a member of the Municipal Party Committee, presided over the meeting and reported on the significance of Children's Day. Afterwards, Wu Xiongcheng, a student from Henghe Elementary School, gave a speech. After the commemoration, students from Shuiting, Tai Miao Xiang, Zhongzheng Bridge, Gao Yinxiang and other elementary schools performed for entertainment. The Municipal Party Committee distributed commemorative badges, and the National Goods Exhibition and National Goods Factories donated a large number of domestic children's products. At 2:00 PM, the Provincial Folk Education Center held a children's free painting competition, with prizes awarded to each participant.

Ministry of Education Orders Provincial and Municipal Departments to Expedite Primary Education Statistics 171

(Nanjing, 4th) The Ministry of Education ordered the provincial and municipal departments of education, stating that the national primary education statistics for the 19th year have been compiled and printed. The order instructed them to conduct detailed research and comparison of the state of primary education in their provinces to seek improvement. The Ministry of Education is now combining the national primary education statistics for the 20th and 21st years and instructed them to fill out and submit the statistical forms previously issued by the Ministry for these two years so that they can be compiled. The order also said the reporting procedures should be expedited as much as possible while striving for accuracy to avoid future difficulties in correcting errors.

Gengzi Indemnity Funds and Educational and Cultural Undertakings in Various Countries (4) 172

Belgian Gengzi Indemnity 173

1. Motivation for Returning the Funds

The Belgian Gengzi indemnity refund movement is actually a branch of the Sino-French education movement. In the second year of the Republic, Li Yuzhi and the French Doctor Delamare founded the Society for Thrifty Study in France to introduce students to study in France. Some of them were transferred to study in Belgium. Later, Cai Yuanpei, Wang Zhaoming, Li Yuying, and the French men Eurard, Moudai, and Delamare founded the Sino-French Education Association to introduce more and more students to study in Belgium, especially at the Ecole Ouvriere Superieure (Xiaoluohai Workers' University). The idea of refunding the funds to promote education became increasingly prominent.

2. The Mature Period for Returning the Funds

In the seventh year of the Republic, the national education community launched a campaign to request various countries to return the funds. At that time, Cai Yuanpei, president of Peking University, and others initiated the campaign in the north, sending commissioners to Europe to negotiate, paying particular attention to Belgium. The southwest also entrusted Wang Zhaoming, Li Yuying, Zhang Ji, and others to go to Europe to investigate education, focusing on the refund of funds from France and Belgium. After the eighth year of the Republic, Chu Minyi, the correspondent of Peking University in Europe, continued the efforts. It happened that Professor Surlet of the University of Brussels advocated the idea of returning the funds to promote education, and Jellot, the president of the Xiaoluohai University, also advocated jointly establishing a Sino-Belgian University with China and requested the Belgian government to subsidize the funds and hoped for the return of the funds. In the ninth year of the Republic, Chu Minyi and Xiao Yu negotiated with Jellot again, surveyed the site near the Labour University of Xiaoluohai, and established a Chinese student dormitory to establish the foundation for the Sino-Belgian University. Soon, Mr. Xiao returned to China and reported this to the authorities of Peking University and the Sino-French University Office in Beijing, both of which received enthusiastic support. In the winter of that year, the Guangdong Provincial Government donated 120,000 francs and remitted them to be used for the opening and equipment of the Sino-Belgian University. In the tenth year of the Republic, the educational associations of Hunan and Zhili provinces initiated a joint petition of the national academic community to friendly countries to return the funds for education, with 43,000 people signing the petition. In the winter of the eleventh year, Xiao Yu was sent to Belgium again as a representative to submit the petition. Wang Jingqi, the Chinese ambassador to Belgium, also assisted in the promotion. Before long, Lefu, the Belgian Minister of Education, Chaspar, the Minister of Foreign Affairs, Frank, the Minister of Colonies, Destere, a member of the Parliament, and Franki, a minister of state and president of the National Bank, successively supported the proposal, and the refund of the funds was successful.

3. Exchange of Notes between China and Belgium

In the fourteenth year of the Republic, the Beijing government and the Belgian ambassador to China consulted several times. On September 5 of that year, the governments of China and Belgium established an exchange of notes to resolve the Belgian part of the Gengzi indemnity. The content was roughly as follows: the Chinese government acknowledged that the balance of the Belgian part of the Gengzi indemnity, amounting to 29,053,611 francs and 15 centimes, from September 1, 1925 to the end of December 1940, would be calculated according to the telegraphic transfer method adopted in 1905. The Sino-Belgian Bank would advance the funds and pay them to the Belgian government in one lump sum. The Chinese government should order the Inspector General of Customs to first repay the Sino-Belgian Bank's advance funds on a monthly basis from the customs revenue starting from September 1, 1925. After the advance funds were repaid, the funds paid monthly by the Inspector General of Customs would be handed over to the Sino-Belgian Committee for Sino-Belgian educational, charitable, public and public works projects. According to this agreement, all funds delivered by the Inspector General of Customs to the Sino-Belgian Bank should be issued as a US dollar bond with a total amount of US$5,605,991.42 (This is the pure principal of the Chinese government's debt to Belgium). The total amount of principal and interest listed on the individual bonds would be US$9,044,402.68 (This is the pure principal of the Chinese government's debt to Belgium plus the estimated interest). The advance funds that should be repaid to the Sino-Belgian Bank had already been repaid in full by May 1927. The remaining Gengzi indemnity due in that month was US$23,541.56.

4. Second Sino-Belgian Agreement

According to the original agreement (i.e., the first agreement), the funds remaining after the repayment of the advance funds should be handed over to the Sino-Belgian Committee for safekeeping and allocation. The Chinese and Belgian governments specially consulted on the matter in December 1927. As a result, the remaining funds from May 1927, together with the indemnity for ten months from June 1927 to March 1928, were allowed to be used by the Chinese government to withdraw from customs. Of this amount, US$100,000 should be set aside for repatriation and relief of Belgian nationals. All customs revenue received monthly from April 1, 1928, to December 31, 1940, would be used as security for the issuance of US dollar bonds. The funds would be allocated as follows: 40% to the Longhai Railway for the purchase of materials from Belgium, 35% to other Chinese state-owned railways for the purchase of materials from Belgium, and 25% for Sino-Belgian educational and charitable undertakings. The repayment period for this Gengzi indemnity was originally scheduled to end at the end of December 1940, but after this agreement, it was changed to end at the end of October 1941.

5. Organization of the Belgian Gengzi Indemnity Committee

The Belgian Gengzi Indemnity Committee is named the Sino-Belgian Gengzi Indemnity Committee. This committee is organized by representatives selected by the Chinese and Belgian governments. The Chinese representatives consist of six people dispatched by the Ministries of Education, Foreign Affairs, Internal Affairs, Finance, Health, and Railways, called regular members. Each ministry may also dispatch one deputy representative, called a deputy member. The Belgian side consists of three regular representatives and six deputy representatives. Each side has one chairman and one vice-chairman. In the general assembly, each delegation has only one vote, regardless of the number of attendees. All resolutions must be unanimously agreed upon by the two delegations. The term of office of the committee members is five years. The authority of this committee is based on the second Sino-Belgian agreement to allocate funds for Sino-Belgian academic and charitable undertakings.

6. Current Committee Members

The Chinese chairman is Chu Minyi, and the regular members are Zeng Zongjian, Li Zhaohuan, Zhu Shiquan, Cai Hong, and Kong Lixing. The deputy members are Shen Pengfei, Jiang Fu, Chen Tieshan, Chen Dasan, Jin Baoshan, and Ye Jinghua. The Belgian chairman is Lambert, the vice-chairman is Wzzerde, and the regular members are Herj and Huberl. The deputy members are Renard, Demeeter, Lafantaine, Devleeschouwer, Capelle Henrzde Favean. Chu Minyi, Zeng Zongjian, Lambert, and Hers are permanent members.

7. Recent Allocation of Belgian Gengzi Indemnity

When various Gengzi Indemnity agencies met last November, the Sino-Belgian Gengzi Indemnity Committee submitted a statement of final accounts for the 22nd year, which is recorded as follows:

(A) Under Educational Undertakings

Tuition Fund for Studying in Belgium US$220,000 in bonds

Schools in Mongolia, Shanxi, and Ningxia US$80,000 in bonds

Schools in Chahar US$40,000 in bonds

Schools in Hubei US$20,000 in bonds

Sino-Belgian Exchange Cultural Lectures US$30,000 in bonds

(B) Under Health Undertakings

The above totals US$1,157,200 in bonds and US$115,000 in cash.

The above allocations are for US dollar bonds and cash owned by the Committee.

In addition, there are funds that can be received as follows:

1. One-fourth of the remaining funds payable by Customs in accordance with Article 4 of the Sino-Belgian Agreement of December 8, 1927, to the Committee (The Committee can obtain one-fourth of this amount, which is RMB 58,023.60 per month) from February 1941 to November 1941.

2. US$80,000 borrowed by the Pinghan Railway and Lincheng Coal Mine should be repaid.

3. 5% interest on the US$3.75 million appropriated by the Ministry of Railways to the Committee (but has not yet been paid).

4. Various interest and unpaid funds (which can be used as working capital).

British Boxer Indemnity Funds 174

1. Motivation for Refund

The idea of ​​refunding the British Boxer Indemnity Funds came later, around after the Great War. At that time, the British government (1) recognized the remarkable achievements of the United States in managing education with refunded funds, (2) was influenced by the Allies allowing China to suspend payment of indemnity funds for five years during the Great War, and (3) was moved by the enthusiasm of both the government and the public in China for refunding the indemnity funds. Therefore, it intended to return the Boxer Indemnity Funds to China for the benefit of both countries. Around 1918, Wang Xueting, Liang Long, Ren Kainan, Chen Yuan and other students studying in the UK published a booklet requesting the UK to refund the indemnity funds, and contacted the British government, parliament, and education circles. Many parties expressed sympathy. At the same time, the domestic education circles launched a "Same Standard" movement, and entrusted Tao Menghe and others, who were going to Europe to study post-war education, to lobby the British. Since then, British figures such as Russell, Lewis, and Giles have written articles in British newspapers and magazines advocating the refund, which attracted public attention.

2. Maturity Period of Refund

In 1922, students studying in the UK organized the Boxer Indemnity Funds for Education Committee, with Yang Ziyu as chairman, Chen Baorong as secretary, and Zhang Daofan, Deng Yousheng, Huang Jianzhong, Liu Zhaoming, Pan Shaotang and others as members, to jointly carry out activities at home and abroad. Initially, they only wrote articles, gave speeches, and published booklets to promote the refund to members of the British Parliament, education circles, and the press. Later, they invited Cai Yuanpei, a famous Chinese educator in Europe, to go to the UK to advocate for the refund. After Cai arrived in London, with the assistance of Zhu Zhaoxin, the acting Chinese representative in the UK, and all the students studying in the UK, he made strong contacts with the British government and the public. He also gave a speech on [The Development of Chinese Education] at the China Society, hosted by the British, emphasizing that the new China would soon rise and desperately needed scientific education, hoping that the British would provide moral and economic assistance (referring to the refund of the indemnity funds for education). He also submitted a written opinion to the British Parliament, clearly stating that the refund should be used for education as a permanent memorial. Subsequently, Cai made the same appeal in the Liverpool area, which was greatly appreciated by British government officials and the public. In the winter of 1922, the British government formally declared that the remaining Boxer Indemnity Funds due to be paid by China would be returned to China for education, culture, and mutually beneficial projects between the two countries. However, due to the British parliamentary elections and frequent cabinet changes, the matter was put on hold until June 1925, when the British Parliament formally passed the [Chinese Indemnity Funds Bill], which completely confirmed the matter. Subsequently, considering the need for prior research on the use of the funds, an advisory committee was established, with eleven members, eight from the UK and three from China. In 1926, the committee organized a delegation consisting of Lord Willingdon, Dame Anne Anderson, Professor Soothill, Ding Wenjiang, Hu Shi, and Zeng Chun, to investigate and collect opinions on the use of the refunded funds in various parts of China. At the end of the same year, the delegation prepared a report and recommendations, the content of which was very important. Later, the exchange of notes between the two countries was based on this.

3. Central Government's Exchange of Notes

In September 1930, China and the UK formally signed an exchange of notes, returning the British Boxer Indemnity Funds due to be paid from December 1, 1922, to the Chinese government for management. The Chinese government agreed to use all of these funds as a foundation for educational and cultural undertakings, in accordance with the opinions of the delegation of the advisory committee. Later, the plan was slightly changed, and a portion of the existing and future Boxer Indemnity Funds was borrowed to reorganize and build Chinese railways and other productive enterprises, using the interest to fund educational and cultural undertakings. The recommendation of the advisory committee was adopted to organize a board of directors to manage and allocate the entire Boxer Indemnity Funds. The Chinese government also transferred all existing funds to the London Purchasing Committee, established in London, to purchase bridges, locomotives, vehicles, steel rails, and other materials from British factories for use in Chinese state-owned railways and other productive enterprises. It was stipulated that the refunded funds accumulated from December 1, 1922, to April 1931, totaled £3,504,122 7s 7d, and would be kept by the London Purchasing Committee for the British Boxer Indemnity Funds, which was affiliated to the board of directors. The British Minister to China would hand over half of the Boxer Indemnity Funds that gradually came due to the committee and half to the London Purchasing Committee.

4. Total Amount of British Boxer Indemnity Funds Refunded and Principles for Borrowing and Allocation

The total amount of British Boxer Indemnity Funds to be refunded was £11,186,547 12s, including interest. The amount of Boxer Indemnity Funds due each year varied. This year it was about £596,481. The principles for borrowing and allocation have been stipulated by the Central Political Council, with two-thirds borrowed for the construction and reorganization of railways, and one-third borrowed for water conservancy, electrical and other construction projects (this one-third is divided into 40% for the Huai River Commission, 20% for the Guangdong River Management Committee, and the remaining 40% for (1) developing electrical industries, (2) managing the Yellow River water conservancy, and (3) developing basic industries, each receiving one-third). The annual interest rate for the loans is 5%.

5. Amount of Funds Allocated to Educational and Cultural Undertakings

The British Boxer Indemnity Funds have not been refunded for long, and not many funds have been loaned to various agencies. The interest earned is not enough to be used for educational and cultural undertakings. However, two principles have been established for the use and allocation of interest: (1) It should be used for educational and cultural buildings with permanent commemorative significance and important national cultural undertakings, and should not be used to subsidize the regular or temporary expenses of any agency. (2) Proper allocation should be given to both the central government and various cultural centers across the country, so as to concentrate resources, popularize results, and supplement the shortcomings of domestic education and culture.

6. Board of Directors Organization

The British Boxer Indemnity Funds Committee is officially named the Board of Trustees for the Administration of the Returned Boxer Indemnity Funds. The board has fifteen directors, two-thirds from China and one-third from the UK, appointed by the National Government of the Republic of China and subordinate to the Executive Yuan. Their term of office is three years, with the first term being five people each for one, two, and three years, determined by drawing lots. There is one chairman, appointed by the Chinese government, and one vice-chairman, elected by the directors. Their duties are to manage and allocate the British Boxer Indemnity Funds. Board meetings require the attendance of more than half of the directors, and resolutions must be approved by more than half of the directors present to be valid.

7. Current Board Members

The Chinese members are Zhu Jiahua, Li Shuhua, Li Siguang, Ye Gongchuo, Liu Ruiheng, Song Ziliang, Chen Qicai, Zeng Rongpu, Zeng Yangfu, and Yan Deqing. The British members are Hughes, Massy, ​​Corder, Turner, and Brown. Zhu Jiahua is also the chairman, and Massy is also the vice-chairman.

8. Recent Distribution of British Boxer Indemnity Funds

Recently, not much of the British Boxer Indemnity Funds has been loaned to domestic railways, water conservancy, electrical and other construction projects. As of the end of last year, the interest received was only more than 500,000 yuan in national currency, so it has not yet begun to be distributed. According to the recent budget submitted by the Board of Trustees for the Administration of the Returned Boxer Indemnity Funds, only the expenses for sending students to study in the UK are included, totaling 229,000 yuan in national currency. In addition, there are only the daily expenses of the committee, and the rest has not been used.

Opening of the 3rd Zhejiang Provincial Scout Rally 175

Opening Ceremony in the Morning, Various Competitions in the Afternoon

| Luo Xiatian, Chen Bulei and Others Speak |

Opening Ceremony: The 3rd Zhejiang Provincial Scout Rally was held yesterday (4th) for the first day. The opening ceremony was held at the Provincial Stadium in Meidong Gaoqiao, Hangzhou at 10:00 AM. A total of 81 troops and more than 2,400 scouts were present. Chiang Kai-shek, the chairman of the rally, cancelled his trip to Hangzhou due to the urgent work of suppressing bandits and sent Chiang Jianren as his representative. Vice-Chairmen Chen Bulei and Luo Xiatian, inspectors Fang Qingru, Wang Tingyang, Zheng Wenli, Zeng Yangfu, Zhou Xiangxian, etc., competition referees Zhang Zhongren, Xu Guanyu, Zeng Gansheng, etc., production referees Gai Qixin, Lu Dianyang, Chen Chengren, and art referees Luo Dixian and Hu Douwen, etc., all arrived at the venue earlier. At 10:00 AM, cannons were fired to start the meeting, and the ceremony was held. Luo Xiatian, chairman of the Provincial Executive Committee, gave the opening speech. Fang Qingru, representative of the Central Party Headquarters, and Jiang Jianren, representative of Chairman Chiang, gave speeches. Vice-Chairman Chen Bulei and Xue Yuanlong, representative of the Scout General Association, etc., gave speeches, stating that scouts are disciplined, organized youth, and the lifeblood of the nation. Those who receive scout life training are practicing the New Life Movement. Therefore, young scouts are the hope of the country and the nation, and should take national rejuvenation as their responsibility. At that time, it was raining heavily, but the scouts were full of spirit, standing still and listening. At 12:00, the inspection ceremony was held. At 1:00 PM, photos were taken and the ceremony was completed. In the afternoon, due to the cloudy weather and rain, there were not many spectators, but the various scout competitions continued as planned. A lantern parade was held in the evening. Tomorrow (5th) morning and afternoon will still be various competitions, and a bonfire party will be held in the evening. On the morning of the 6th, the closing ceremony will be held, and various outdoor and water activities will be held in the afternoon.

Activities: The activities are divided into five categories: A. Life competition, divided into four items: food, clothing, housing, and transportation; B. Skills competition, divided into nineteen items: first aid, semaphore, bridge building, platform building, knot tying, fire starting, shooting, surveying, reconnaissance, sewing, climbing, cooking, and music; C. Production exhibition; D. Art exhibition; E. Other activities, divided into nine items: inspection, parade, bonfire, lantern, boating, climbing, service, visit, and meeting.

A Glimpse of the Campground: The campground is divided into twenty areas, with thirty campsites. The management office is in the middle, and the public security bureau, first aid station, dispatch station, health bureau, information center, newspaper office, bank, post office, consumer cooperative, and bookstore are around the outer edge. The inner edge is for production exhibitions and the display of art competition entries. Each troop displayed no less than 10,000 exhibits.

Visiting Scouts: Those who came to Hangzhou to visit the conference included the Scout Training Class of Shanghai Datong Middle School, Shanghai Middle School, Jinan Middle School, Dongya Physical Education College, Zhaohe, Fudan, Jinan, Kaiming, Qingxin, Liangjiang, YMCA, Patriotic Private School, the Joint Visiting Group of Scout Schools in Beijing, and Nantong Middle School, etc.

Ministry of Education Sends Personnel to Inspect Shanxi Education Report 176

Education Funds Not Yet Independent

The Ministry of Education recently sent personnel to inspect education in Shanxi Province. The results of the inspection have been submitted to the Ministry of Education. The following is a detailed account of the opinions on the improvements to be made in Shanxi education in the report:

| Regarding Higher Education |

(1) The amount of higher education funding should be separated from the funding for the attached middle school when compiling the budget from the 23rd academic year onwards. The departments and specialties established should also implement the price calculation plan. If the staffing exceeds the budget, efforts should be made to terminate it. (2) The College of Engineering of Shanxi University must increase equipment as the first step in rectification. The provincial government should allocate temporary funding of 100,000 yuan starting in the 23rd academic year, which can be paid in two installments. The list of equipment to be increased should be compiled by the president of the university with a plan and a list of the number of items and price list submitted to the Ministry for record. (3) The merger of the Provincial Law School and the College of Education into Shanxi University should be handled quickly in accordance with the order and submitted to the Ministry for verification. (4) Technical colleges should concentrate their efforts to expand practice grounds. Subsequently, the establishment of specialties must obtain academic liaison with the part of the attached middle school that is being transformed into vocational schools in order to complete its industrial manufacturing system. (5) Commercial colleges should change the way students practice, paying attention to commercial surveys, commodity research, transportation methods, tax regulations, market conditions, etc., to prepare for future employment.

| Regarding General Education |

(1) It is found that the province's vocational education funding only accounts for 3% of the secondary education funding, which is far from the standard set by the Ministry. In addition to the order to gradually close down the National Normal School and to convert the attached middle schools of the technical and commercial colleges into vocational schools and to stop recruiting students for the attached middle schools of agricultural colleges, so as to transfer the savings to vocational education funding, the report submitted by Gu Zhaohua, the Ministry's inspector, provides a table of the annual distribution and amount of secondary education funding in Shanxi Province. It is estimated that the standard set by the Ministry can be reached in the 26th academic year. The department should carefully review this and use it as a basis. If there are any matters that are not fully covered, the department should recompile it in the same format and submit it to the Ministry for verification. (2) The province's education funding has not yet been independent, and there is no designated special fund for education. The department should invite the presidents of provincial schools and colleges to jointly investigate and study the independent education funding plan, first seeking to determine the special fund and then submit it to the provincial government for implementation. (3) The province's promotion of the laws and regulations issued by the Ministry is still diligent, but there are still areas that need to be earnestly implemented. They should be implemented in accordance with the following points: 1. The names of provincial middle schools, normal schools, and vocational schools should be based on the location in accordance with the regulations. Except for the three locations of Taiyuan Girls' Junior High School, Changzhi Girls' Junior High School, and Yuncheng Girls' Junior High School, which have already been changed, the National Normal School will temporarily retain its original name. The other schools should be corrected separately as listed in the attached table. 2. All existing co-educational junior high schools should be changed to joint schools, retaining the original names of Yangxing, Hefen, Huze, Jiangyuan Puban, etc., in order to comply with the regulations and avoid frequent changes. 3. Private senior high schools in the provincial capital charge students fees without any standards. The Department of Education should consider the situation and re-regulate them to ensure that they do not exceed the maximum limit stipulated by the Ministry, so as to correct them. 4. Local primary schools generally lack contact, and most do not have organizations for primary school research associations. Efforts should be made to supervise and promote them, starting with areas with developed education. 5. There are many omissions in the statistics of various middle schools and normal schools, and many tables and books are also lacking and incomplete. Orders should be issued to prepare them for application. 6. The naming of primary schools in various counties has not yet been changed. The Department of Education should instruct its subordinates to quickly correct them in accordance with the provisions of Article 10 of the Primary School Regulations in order to achieve uniformity. (4) The establishment and management of joint and county junior high schools in the province should be handled in accordance with the following points: 1. The standard for the establishment of junior high schools should be determined by the number of students that senior high schools, normal schools, and vocational schools can accommodate, and should not exceed one-third of the number of students that can be accommodated at most. 2. The surplus classes in junior high schools should be gradually reduced, and the savings should be used to convert them into vocational or other types of schools | or to designate a certain junior high school to be completely converted, or to concentrate the savings to establish new schools, which will be presided over by the Department of Education. 3. The savings in the previous item can be transferred to equipment costs, but they must be approved by the Department of Education. 4. The Department of Education should consider the circumstances and formulate a rectification plan for each junior high school. (5) The province's Taiyuan City has made great achievements in promoting compulsory education. The implementation method of the short-term system is very appropriate. In the future, attention should be paid to the promotion of experimental districts in various counties. (6) The private senior high schools in the province are concentrated in the provincial capital, and the management situation is very inconsistent. They should be earnestly reorganized in accordance with the opinions of the Ministry's inspectors. (7) In the future, the development of vocational education in Shanxi should correspond to the province's construction plan. The points that should be noted should be handled with reference to the inspection opinions.

Chinese Medical Association Continues Meeting 179

The annual meeting of the Chinese Medical Association was held for the second day at 9:00 AM on the 3rd in Beijing. More than 300 members attended. Zhu Shou'nan chaired the meeting. The secretary, Zhu Hengbi, reported three points: (1) 100,000 yuan is needed to build the association's headquarters on the tennis court of the Shanghai Astronomical Observatory in the autumn of this year, and half of the funds are still lacking. Please donate. (2) Please make efforts to introduce members. (3) Please submit articles to the Chinese Medical Journal. All members passed the acceptance and donated 1,300 yuan on the spot. Then a general meeting was held, chaired by Mei Yilin. Members reported on papers on public health. At noon, the Shen Bao hosted a banquet. In the afternoon, group meetings were held and papers were read. At 6:00 PM, the city government hosted a reception and visited the Five Continents Park. At 7:00 PM, Dean Wang hosted a banquet at the Lizhi Society.

(Nanjing, 4th) The Chinese Medical Association continued its meeting on the 4th at 9:00 AM. More than 300 members attended. Zhu Shou'nan chaired the meeting. The secretary first read the minutes of the general meeting on the 3rd. Then the Research Committee and the Health Committee reported on the progress of their work. The Health Committee formulated a two-year plan, divided into five groups, to conduct research on public health surveys in modern urban and rural areas, etc. A Pre-Tuberculosis Association was also established in Shanghai, with Niu Huisheng and others responsible for carrying out the work. The association's articles of association were discussed, and six members were elected, as well as matters such as property fundraising. The term of office is six years. The president and vice-president are elected from among those who are well-known, virtuous, and have made significant contributions to the association's affairs. The meeting adjourned at noon. In the afternoon, all members visited Zijin Mountain and visited the Astronomical Observatory and the Meteorological Research Institute. The association's next general meeting will be held in Guangdong.

Jiangsu Province County Education Bureaus to Send New Education Budget 183

Before the 18th year of the Republic, the income and expenditure of education funds in various counties in Jiangsu Province were generally without a budget, resulting in insufficient actual income. Counties such as Jiangdu, Gaoyou, and Baoying often accumulated debts due to the lack of standards for expenditure. After the establishment of the Department of Education, the compilation of education budget was considered very important, as this was the only way to prevent waste and urged it very strictly. If the income of education funds in various counties does not change, it can gradually reach a stable state. The new education budget for the 23rd year of the Republic was originally limited to the end of March for compilation and submission for approval. The county education bureaus that have compiled and submitted them to the county governments for submission to the department include Shanghai, Huaian, and Gaoyou. More than a dozen counties have also sent letters to the fourth section of the Department of Education stating that they have compiled them and are waiting for the Education and Administration Committee to review them before submitting them for approval. It is estimated that the education budget for the 23rd year of the Republic of various counties can be submitted to the department by the end of this month.

Special Feature

Boy Scout Education by Zheng Xiaocang 188

Boy Scout education is a youth education full of life. It is an education of proactive health, an education of understanding nature, an education that emphasizes mutual assistance and cooperation, and an education that cultivates law-abiding attitudes and enterprising spirit.

It utilizes the tendency for activity, the tendency for gregariousness, and the tendency for [blank space] during youth, guiding them to strive for good and progress positively.

The Boy Scouts were first established in 1908 (four years before the founding of the Republic of China). In just over twenty years, there are already more than two million Boy Scouts worldwide. Furthermore, recent methods of youth training in various countries seem to be derived from this.

The Boy Scouts are a major contribution of the British nation to education. Although Duke Baden-Powell does not have a specialized book on educational theory, he has such a profound understanding of education. No wonder Dr. Snaedt (Professor of Education at Columbia University) often sighs that he is a "genius of education." I think his contribution to youth education is likely to be as great as Froebel's contribution to elementary education.

I have two hopes here:

(1) Education in middle schools should adopt its entire spirit and part of its method. This is "education for life." This is an education that promotes creating a "new life" and a new nation.

(2) If there is a way to extend it to young people in agriculture, industry, and commerce, with simple and inexpensive clothing and meaningful training, it would be a boon to the nation. Even if it is only an ideal at this time, realizing the ideal should be a goal for those who serve in the Boy Scouts and those engaged in social education.
